		<username>balaenaglacialis</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>"Terabithia . . . enthralls and absorbs the viewer in the magic of imagination and the reality of every-day life.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Review: By Morgan StewartIt is hard to put into writing just how marvelous and wonderful Bridge to Terabithia really is, yet as I attempt it, I can't help feeling disturbed at how ridiculous people are being about the marketing of this film. Thank goodness most real critics have looked past the agreeably deceptive marketing, into the heart and beauty of this film, which, with or with the misleading advertisements is impressive. After seeing it, I struggled to think of a better way of marketing this film, without giving away its ending or taking away the only audience that still seems to watch PG movies, kids.After watching it, however, I couldn't imagine taking anyone under ten to see it, nor could I imagine anyone under ten enjoying it as much as young adults, or even older audiences would. So, as deceptive as the advertising was, I myself realize that the fascinating story, the charm and skill of the actors, and the good direction of newcomer to live action film-making, Gabor Csupo, more than makes up for the slightly skewed first impressions. And I am eternally grateful that it did not turn into what everyone seemed to want, a cheesy Narnia rip-off. If anything, the movie was a lot better than the preview made it seem to be, and I was pleasantly surprised.Instead of the brash and rude approach to filming movies, that seems to be the standard today with effects driven movies, Terabithia focuses on the characters, the story, and the heart when telling this beautiful tale. Which, is part of the reason why I enjoyed it so much. Too often now days the story is built around the effects, not around the characters. A rather cumbersome and annoying way to tell a story, or be told a story, if you ask me. Instead, Terabithia uses the talents of both the amazing young actors, and its adult cast to enthrall and absorb the viewer in the magic of imagination and the reality of every-day life.The story focuses on young Jess Aarons, whose school life and home life aren't all that ideal. He deals with bullies at school, and four sisters at home. Josh Hutcherson, who I haven't particularly enjoyed before, plays the part of Jess perfectly, his emotions and reactions spot on, throughout.What is a school without the new girl? Leslie Burke, played by AnnaSophia Robb, takes on the part of the imaginative and friendly new girl and brings to Jess gifts of imagination and friendship. Robb truly does a superb job in bringing to life the thoughtful and imaginative Leslie Burke.All of the supporting cast was also brilliantly portrayed. I especially enjoyed the performances of Robert Patrick as Jess's father, and young Bailee Madison as Jess's little sister May Belle.Together, Jess and Leslie create a world to call their own. A place that no one else can get to, a place in their imaginations. Terabithia, a land of beautiful creatures and dangerous enemies, springs forth from their imaginations, and becomes a place to call their own, away from the bullies and monotony of everyday life.What really struck me as brilliant was the limited, yet still perfect number of glimpses into the children's' imaginations. We don't see a lot of Terabithia, which is good, because it is more about the journey of the characters, than the land of Terabithia. That said, it still has quite a few more scenes of adventure than the book by Katherine Patterson, all of which add to, not take away from the story.The writing, also is quite good. David Patterson, son of the novel's author takes great care when adapting the beloved work of his mother into a screenplay. Most of the lines from the book aren't there, but there are a few which make it in, revealing the care and love that was put into the scripting of this movie. Personally, I enjoy the screenplay of the movie more than the words of the book, but that is just my opinion. The movie's script greatly aided in the believability of the characters, and the motion of the scenes, which were crisp and well-planned.The movie touched on my every emotion, bringing me to tall peaks of happiness and leaving me teary-eyed and disconsolate, but still had a perfect and satisfying ending. I also, personally thought, the scenes and situations were more powerful, poignant, and realistic, than the book, which surprises me. Usually, the movie can't live up to the book. In this case, the phrase seemed switched around. The book didn't live up to the movie. As weird as it is for me to say this about a movie, Terabithia touched my heart like no film has ever before. And I doubt any film will give me quite the same feeling, ever again.</fullReview>
	</review>

It REALLY outclasses any number of recent movies marketed at kids and it is one of the few I've seen that shows honest portrayals of both children and adults. No one, not even the bullies, is a stereotype or caricature. The novel is a masterpiece, but this film holds its own. With so many films, you walk out, whether amused or annoyed, and soon forget most of what you saw. Not so with Bridge--it stays with you, as it should. Go and enjoy...and then pass the word.</fullReview>

		<username>tollini</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Truly Moving Picture</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I saw this film on January 23rd, 2007 in Indianapolis. I am one of the judges for the Heartland Film Festival's Truly Moving Picture Award. A Truly Moving Picture "?explores the human journey by artistically expressing hope and respect for the positive values of life." Heartland gave that award to this film.This is a story of a poor 10-year old boy who wants to be the fastest boy in his class at school. To his surprise, the new girl who moves in next door to him beats him out fair and square and wins the race. This is no way to start a relationship or friendship.However, they have something in common. They are both being bullied at school. And they each react differently. The boy, Jesse, is passive and tries to stay out of harm's way. The girl, Leslie, is aggressive and challenges her tormentors. Who knows what the right way is to fight bullying, but they find their defense in friendship with each other. And, they find a wonderful way to experience this trying time in life via their vivid imagination and the creation of a magical and enchanting kingdom that is very real to them.They are both creative people. He is an artist and she is a writer. These creative people are able to close their eyes, picture another world, and keep their minds open to fantastic visions.But the bullying persists and they attempt to come to grips with their pain in various ways. They try to out smart their tormentors and do, but they don't enjoy being bullies and becoming like their enemies. This story is based on a Newbery-winning novel. It is a child's story. But, it is also a story for adults. It will bring you emotionally to your knees. It is lovingly and professionally told, and the fantasy part of the story ? the magical kingdom ? is wonderfully and briefly shown on the screen. This keeps the story grounded and believable.Jesse and Leslie are beautiful people regardless of their ages. They show us how to enjoy life, how to do the right things, how to be faithful to one's friends, and have hope for the future. We learn a lot from these ten year old children. FYI ? There is a Truly Moving Pictures web site where there is a listing of past Truly Moving Picture Award winners that are now either at the theater or available on video.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>Nez-Alpha</username>
		<score>0.7</score>
		<shortDescription>Story over effects.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>When I sat down to watch Bridge to Terabithia, I did not know quite what to expect. From what I had seen in the trailers, I thought the movie would be about two kids that end up in some magical world, similar to the Chronicles of Narnia (clearly, I did not read the book). Needless to say that I was surprised when actually seeing the movie. I shall not spoil the story for those who have yet to see the movie, but I will say that, in my opinion, this movie is for a more mature audience than one would think. Rather than being a fairytale for youngsters, the movie actually gives the viewer an inside look in a young boy's life and all the troubles he faces, concerning school, family and friends. The setting overall was a lot darker than expected as well. I can be short about the acting. The child-stars that play the lead roles did a great job and really brought the characters to life. On this subject I must give some credit to the director as well, as it is very difficult to work with children and to get them to play the part exactly the way you want them too. One final aspect of the movie that deserves mentioning is the fact that it does not lean on special effects. Although there is a fair amount of nice CGI present in the film, the story dominates. Which in my opinion, is a lot better than the other way around. Overall, I found the movie very enjoyable, but I would advise parents of young children to find out more about the movie, before deciding on whether or not you'll let your kids watch it.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>Close your eyes, but keep your mind wide open . . .</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Bridge To TerabithiaI have not read the book and did not see this movie with many expectations. To begin with, this is a story of Jesse Aarons (Josh Hutcherson). Jesse is the fastest runner in his class and very proud of being so. Frequently picked on by the local bullies, troubled with the financial situation back home and oft ignored by all but one of his 5 sisters, he immerses himself within his drawings as an escape... Leslie Burke (AnnaSophia Robb)is the new-kid in his class. She has a panache for writing which coupled by her ability to outrun all the guys in her class (including Jesse) ensures that she doesn't have the best luck making new friends. However, with their affinity to be picked on, Jesse and Leslie soon find themselves extremely fond of each other and off looking for a place of their own... This is Terabithia...And this is where I'll end my summary for I do not wish to go into the spoilers for the movie.All the kids in the movie really shine in their respective roles. As many reviewers have said before me, Josh and AnnaSophia are a wonderful pair! I would also like to mention the young Bailee Madison (playing Josh's younger sister) for her portrayal of May Belle. However, what truly lifts this movie from "good" to "great" is the simplicity of the whole story. This is a children's movie through and through and but do not expect a typical Disney feel-good comedy. Do not also expect huge CG sequences like say, The Chronicles of Narnia.This movie is full of heart and everything about it is shown from the eyes of a child. Life, is not a pretty thing and more than the magical kingdom of Terabithia, this is a tale of a young kids' coming to terms with matters of being bullied, being loved, having a true friend and even trying to understand death.By the end of it all, many people around me were moved to tears and I myself was trying desperately to hold back. The movie, its message and its delivery are all beautiful.On a critical note, the only thing about the movie that I didn't particularly love was the music. The music in general wasn't very well suited and certain songs were just not needed, but I suppose thats what the MTv culture demands.In conclusion, I highly recommend it. Go and watch this movie and if you have them, take your children... They'll love it!9/10</fullReview>

		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>Touching story</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>A very well mastered family movie with a positive message that addresses topical themes for children in a poignant, focused manner. The children depicted are very real and likable (well, except for the ones you're supposed to dislike, that is), and easy to identify with. The movie is a faithful and touching adaptation of the beloved children's classic book.The two main characters, Jesse and Leslie (splendidly played by John Hucheson and Annasophia Robb) are typical pre-teens, steering their way through the routine ups and downs kids everywhere deal with, and they develop a friendship/first crush due to their common interests and challenges. They find an old tree house, and create a fantasy castle type kingdom complete with magic, and populated by creatures based on people they know. Unlike so many other fantasy movies, this world is just an amusement for them, not a refuge that they actually "enter." The animation effects of this fantasy kingdom are skillfully executed in such a manner as to point out the reality that exists alongside the fantasy. For example: a tree begins to move, comes to life and performs an action, then relaxes back into its "real" position.The relationships of all the characters, and what they learn from their experiences, are the true focus, with the fantasy sequences only spicing what's happening. There are many themes touched upon: friendship, tragedy, adventure, creativity, bullies, competition, family life, even making an enemy to a friend. I liked all the characters and the actors that played them; each person helped build the story. Emotional, even heart wrenching in one case, this movie is a gem. Highly recommended.</fullReview>
	</review>

I've been trying to drag my friends there with me because I think that everyone should see this, but unfortunately, the add campaign may have ruined all chances of that happening. I find that every time I ask one of my friends to go with me, they say that there is no way they are going to watch that movie, which means I'll probably have to see it alone when I watch it again (I will definitely be watching this again). It was so good that I cried during the movie. I only remember crying in one other movie ever.Bridge to Terabithia just might be my new favorite movie. I wasn't sure if Spiderman 2 and Serenity would ever be pushed down in ranking, but Bridge to Terabithia is making it a close race.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Very well done, not your average children's movie!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Bridge to Terabithia, based on the book, is a story about two kids, Jess and Leslie, who form a friendship over a shared outcast status at their school. Bullied, they seek their own refuge from the world in the form of their own kingdom, Terabithia.I read a comment about this movie not being for children, and I have to say, I totally disagree. I think this movie is wonderful for adults and children alike. It deals with some major issues in new and creative ways. Jess and Leslie deal with their problems by recreating them in an imaginary world where they can be the things they aren't in real life. This gives them the strength to deal with them in the real world.The more serious issues are handled in a way that parents can appreciate as not too "adult" for their children, and children as not too "grown-up" for them to grasp.Fans of the book will be happy to know that CGI effects do not overshadow the themes of the book, and though they make up a large part of the trailer, they actually make up less than a third of the movie.Kids and adults, be warned : bring the tissues.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Great; *IF* you know what to expect</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Based on the heartbreaking book, BRIDGE TO TERABITHIA strays from the regular family film, while still delivering a strong message.Two words you must remember before seeing this movie, though: FALSE ADVERTISING.Terabithia is NOT another Narnia by any means. It is advertised that way, but it is not what it seems to be. For book fans, however, Terabithia is a great adaption.The acting is amazing; Josh Hutcherson (Little Manhattan) pulls his part off excellently. Josh is one of the best male child stars of this generation, without a doubt. Annasophia Robb (Charlie and the Chocolate Factory) stars in yet another Walden Media film, and, despite her disappointing performance in Because of Winn-Dixie, she gives a great performance. She is able to captivate Leslie's innocence and free-spirited nature without becoming annoying or obnoxious. Putting aside the two wonderful leads, another star shines; The puppy-faced Bailee Madison. Her smile lights up the screen and she is cute without getting on your nerves. She steals every scene she has a line in. The other children and the adults, again, are great and this is what truly makes the movie move along.The moral? Many worried parents seem to have the wrong idea of this movie. I can understand why, but you must look beyond the obvious. This movie does not just make us realize what reality is, but it shows us love, friendship, and courage. It teaches us how to stand up to our enemies and how to make friends; How to love, and how to deal with the issues of everyday life. The movie shows us that love comes in every shape, size, and way, and that a true bond cannot be broken, despite road blocks. The ones you love are always with you.And, with ending this, I will put a quote that most people have heard, but it truly fits this movie; Fairy tales are more than real: Not because they tell us that dragons exist, but that dragons can be defeated.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Cried like a baby, Amazing film.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>About 10 years ago, when I was 8-years-old, a schoolteacher friend of my mother's gave me a book to read, and that book was Bridge to Terabithia. I was absolutely enthralled by the novel, and found myself crying at the end, the first time a work of fiction had made me cry. The magic and wonder of the book stuck with me the past decade, so you can imagine my excitement when I found out it was being turned into a movie!I went in with high expectations and was not in any way disappointed. The movie version of Bridge was incredibly true to the book, and the young actors portraying Leslie and Jess did a fantastic job. One of my favorite parts was Zooey Deschenal as the music teacher, the way she got the kids singing those songs was fabulous, those scenes were my favorites. They were so well done, with the children looking like they truly cared about what they were singing, putting all their feeling into it.The most powerful aspect of the film was the portrayal of the imagination children possess. My friends and I found ourselves crying when Jess finally "kept his mind wide open" as Leslie suggested, and saw Terabithia for the first time. It broke my heart to realize that, at 18, I no longer possess the imagination and creativity that Jess and Leslie did at their young age.Terabithia was shown as the perfect escape mechanism for the two kids, to get away from their bullies and family troubles. It was amazing how their fantasy world, where they were a brave King and Queen, gave them the courage to stand up to their bullies.The moment Jess found out he was going to the museum with his teacher, I broke down, because I knew what was coming. When Jess' father breaks the new of Leslie's death, your heart all but breaks. The scenes that follow can be very difficult to watch, particularly when the kids are next shown in music class, singing a mournful sort of tune very sadly, Jess with his head on his desk, fighting back tears.The movies wraps up beautifully with Jess bringing his ever-present little sister Maybel to Terabithia, having finally built a bridge into he and Leslie's secret kingdom. He tells her she is the princess, and that her subjects, the Terabithians, were all very excited to see her.The whole movie was so powerful, and has a devastating effect on those of us who miss the innocence of childhood, when all one needed to have a good time was the head on their shoulders.10 out of 10.</fullReview>

		<date>2007-04-16</date>
		<username>EricPC5150</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Great adaptation of a beloved book!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Bridge To Terabithia was my favorite book as a kid - I first read it over 25 years ago. It was an amazing, haunting, sad, and powerful story of friendship and loss. It's still one of my favorite books as both an adult and a writer. It has since become a modern classic of children's literature, a book beloved by children and adults alike. It's also one of the most controversial children's books of all time - one of the most banned and challenged.But I never expected it to be made into a feature film. I assumed that the mediocre made-for-TV version would be the only film adaptation made of Bridge To Terabithia, due to its difficult themes. I was absolutely shocked to learn that Disney's Walden Media division was making a feature film. I envisioned a bubblegum monstrosity having almost nothing to do with the book on which it was based.I was never more happy to be wrong in my life! This is a wonderful adaptation of Bridge To Terabithia and very faithful to Katherine Paterson's beautiful, heartbreaking story. That's because the movie was co-produced and co-written by David Paterson, whose real-life childhood tragedy inspired his mother to write the book.Fifth-grader Jess Aarons (Josh Hutcherson) is a poor, introverted, but artistically gifted farm boy living in rural Virginia. He has four sisters. His two older sisters despise him and his younger sisters worship him. With money so tight, Jess's emotionally distant, foul-tempered father spends most of his time working out of town.The only bright spot in Jess's life is his pretty, hip music teacher, Miss Edmunds (Zooey Deschanel), who admires Jess' talent for drawing and encourages him to try and realize his dream of becoming an artist. Jess has a huge, secret crush on her.Jess has no friends, but he hopes to win his peers' admiration by becoming the fastest kid in the fifth grade and winning the big race at recess. Jess is shocked when a new classmate - a girl named Leslie Burke (Annasophia Robb) - decides to join in the boys' race. She ends up beating him and embarrassing him in front of the other boys. That's no way to start a friendship, but soon, Jess and Leslie become inseparable best friends.Leslie is the complete opposite of Jess - she's bright, outgoing, and a fierce nonconformist. She's also creative like Jess - a natural storyteller with a vast imagination. Together, Leslie and Jess create Terabithia, a secret imaginary kingdom in the forest, where they rule as king and queen. It becomes a sanctuary for them, where they are safe from ridicule, the real-life school bullies that persecute them, and the imaginary monsters that Leslie dreams up.To Jess, Leslie is more than just his best friend. She's his soulmate and his reason for living. She took a poor, awkward farm boy and made him a king. For the first time in his life, Jess feels good about himself. With Leslie by his side, he's invincible. She also teaches him important life lessons, like being compassionate to those in need - even if you don't like them.Then suddenly, a terrible, unimaginable tragedy takes Leslie away from Jess forever. Devastated and nearly crushed by the weight of his grief, Jess must summon all the strength Leslie gave him in order to cope with his loss and make the magic of Terabithia - and Leslie's memory - live on.This is one of the all-time great tearjerkers, a story of great emotional depth and power. So bring lots of Kleenex. I'm a grown man now, and I've read the book many times, but I still tear up at the end. The movie is just as powerful, and Josh Hutcherson's superb, emotional performance will melt even the hardest of hearts. Annasophia Robb is magnificent as Leslie. She literally becomes the apotheosis of the character.The supporting cast is excellent as well, especially Robert Patrick as Jess' father - a role that's a far cry from the witty tough guys he usually plays.Beautifully and sensitively directed by animator Gabor Csupo in his first live-action film, Bridge To Terabithia also features a soaring, gorgeous soundtrack by Aaron Zigman. As I said before, the script, by David Paterson and Jeff Stockwell, is very faithful to the book and captures all the emotion of the story. However, I must say that some key scenes of character development in the book are either not in the script, have been changed, or are woefully underdeveloped.If you haven't read the book, I wholeheartedly encourage you to read it after you see the movie. Some fans of the book may complain about the changes and omissions, but I've been a fan for over 25 years, and I think that this is a first-rate adaptation of Bridge To Terabithia.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>InLibrisLibertas</username>
		<score>0.1</score>
		<shortDescription>A decent movie in itself, but horrible as a fantasy and for children</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>To be fair, Bridge to Terabithia is actually quite a nice movie....if you ignore the fact that it is advertised as fantasy and aimed at children. If it were marketed correctly, I would be pressed to give it a MUCH higher rating, but as it stands it is completely inappropriate.I have never read the book so I'll admit that I went willingly into it uninformed, but neither have a lot of other people who made that same decision and I imagine the people in charge of the movie must have realized this. It therefor falls on the previews to accurately portray the content of the film for those of us unfamiliar with the original text, but whoever was responsible for that failed miserably.By the trailers, one would reasonably expect the movie to be something akin to The Chronicles of Narnia: children entering their own miraculous fantasy land, with all sorts of adventure and no shortage of magical creatures.What you get is only a few brief glimpses at anything even remotely whimsical. There are some monster squirrels and a giant troll based off of real life bullies they have problems with at school, and the "Dark Master" who is only ever seen as a black blur running through the trees and never has a direct encounter with any of the characters.The majority of the movie deals with hard life issues, like emotionally distant family members, bullying, isolation, and the harsh reality that you have to grow up and leave your childish fantasies behind sooner or later, that the real word is a rough place and you have to learn to weather it. That's all well and good in a coming-of-age film for older kids, but that is not what it's marketed as or who it's aimed at.The fantasy elements (which we rarely actually get to see) are imagined by the two main characters, Jess and Leslie, as a coping mechanism and never fully developed until the very end of the movie, where Terabithia FINALLY comes alive in its fullest, but we only get to see it for a few seconds before the credits roll.There is a bit somewhere in the middle where they bring up religious commentary out of nowhere, and why they feel the need to do that is anybody's guess as it has very little to do with any part of the movie before that moment. It ends up coming off as awkward and a bit pretentious on the writer's part and probably should have been cut. (Not to speak poorly of religion or Christianity; it just seemed totally out of place here.) But perhaps worst of all is Leslie's death. The movie spends the whole time up to that building her up as a sort of personal savior for Jess. He is alone at school and at home, with nobody to appreciate his love for the arts, until Leslie and her family move in next door and he finally meets a kindred spirit. They fast become best friends and through Leslie, Jess can finally experience happiness. If they had left it at that, this might have been a perfect kids' movie, but instead, near the end of the film, they kill Leslie off out of nowhere while Jess is away on a trip with his teacher at the museum and when he comes home his parents just lay it on him. So not only does he lose the closest person to him at that point, he is not allowed to say goodbye to her and the news that she is gone is dropped on him like a bomb.It is truly and completely tragic. They just keep laying one thing after another on poor Jess until you feel YOU, the viewer from the outside, are going to cave under the feeling of complete and total hopelessness and grief.Now, everyone has to learn to deal with tragedy at some point and it would be perfectly acceptable if the people in charge of advertising had given us fair warning of this ahead of time, but they did no such thing. They made it seem like a bright, fun, fantastic children's movie and then blindsided us with a load of bereavement so overwhelming that it smothers the rest of the film and makes you feel horrible afterward. I am twenty-one years old and well acquainted with these sorts of things, and I was surprised into tears when they killed that sweet little girl. There is no way a little kid would be ready to handle that.I feel as though I was tricked into watching this movie, and it was almost shameful for those in charge to advertise it for young children.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>A shallow, uninteresting attempt at a movie based two elements: child imagination and unexpected tragedy</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Countryside. A young boy and a young girl, living next door. He has troubles in all aspects of life: a poor family which has little to give, bullied as school. She is more fortunate at home - cool, successful parents - so she better tolerates to be bullied at school. The two quickly become best friends. So far, the movie is just average.Now there the first of the two elements of the story: the two elect a piece of wood as an imagined magical world of their own, where they are king and queen. We get to see this world though their imaginative eyes - elves and trolls and whatever. Part of this world clearly mimics the rest of their real lives.Problem is, the movie fails miserably at this element. Both children, but especially her, are far, far too wise. They never really let go of themselves. That's just a lot more boring that any made-up world is supposed to be. Compare with Calvin and Hobbes fantasies. *That* is how a world imagined by a child can look like.The movie here also starts to focus the interior struggle between "let imagination rule" and "get out of your Peter Pan syndrome". The former wins. The movie fails miserably here too: maybe characters are just too flat for that. Fact is, the struggle just look stupid, excessively stylized and plain straightforward.So, now is the time for the second main element of the plot: tragedy strikes. Unexpectedly, she has a random accident and dies. How will everybody, and especially he, react to this? Not too bad, after all. Everybody is just a little sad, her family moves, then life goes on.This tragedy element has little connection with the previous one, and seems just a strong element inserted at random in an attempt to add flavor to this insipid movie. Failure, again. For the second time, character are probably just too flat to produce anything interesting at this point. For an example of a really touching movie that believably and profoundly depicts the tragedy of a missing child, see "Stanza del figlio", by Moretti. The comparison is embarrassing.Summary: the movie is based on two elements with huge potential: unchecked imagination (interesting, full of artistic potential) and death of a child (deeply moving, full of emotional potential). But does a terrible job on both, and at mixing them.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Great concepts, middling execution</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I remember reading this book when I was younger, although my memories of it were quite foggy by the time I got around to watching the movie. Sadly, I cannot say that it was a great movie. Rather, it's a palatable movie that suffers a lot from the shift from book to movie.One thing that really threw me off is the acting of the children. Leslie was very sprite-like, but there was a serious artificiality to her performance that makes it very hard to believe she actually believes what she's saying. Jess on the other hand suffers from only using the acting range that Tom Welling practices on Smallville. That's not to say that Tom Welling's necessarily a limited actor, but that's to say that it's all I see in Jess and that weakens his characterization. Jess' younger sister Maybelle is quite cute and surprisingly believable as the annoying younger sister and most of the other players do a decent job with what little roles they have.I really remember loving the story when I was younger because it related directly to my own imaginative flights of fancy and the real-world portion was also relevant to me at the same time. However, when the story gets translated into a movie format, it drags a lot because, in the book, a lot of the conflict was inside the character rather than outside. And so we get stuck with a lot of brooding scenes (hence the Smallville reference) and not a lot of external conflict (or internal conflict fueling external conflict). With such weak hooks and lack of believability in the actors, it's hard to really get into the picture because there's nothing bringing you in and a whole lot making it hard to be similarly immersed.But it's not bad. In fact, the film shines best in the real world segments because the conflict is much more palpable and there is good drama there. It's just that when you have to suffer through all the less believable flights of fancy (not unbelievable because it's fantastic, but rather, because it's just not well driven or expressed), it really bogs down the film. I personally think a rewrite that reworks the story, or the perspective of the story, might have been good for its screen debut.But it's clean and simple and deals with issues that children sometimes have to face, which I can applaud it for. I just wish it were done in such a way that it drew me better into the story rather than emoting it to me. It's passable. 6/10.</fullReview>

		<date>2007-10-24</date>
		<username>Mel J</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>Delightful coming-of-age film</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>'The Bridge of Terebithia' is an intelligent family film made in the manner of Disney classics like 'Old Yeller' and 'The Fox and the Hound', where things aren't always dressed up prettily just because many in the target audience are children.Based on the novel by Katherine Paterson, this film revolves around twelve-year-old Jesse, the only son of his working class parents' five children. Despite being a gifted artist, he feels insignificant in the midst of four sisters, pre-occupied parents and school bullies until he meets Leslie, a city girl whose family has moved to Jesse's small farming town. Leslie is a bright, outgoing, captivating child with a sense of adventure and a determination to stand out in a crowd yet, in the face of their differences, the two become firm friends. Bouyed by Leslie's genuine enthusiasm for life, Jesse helps her to create the imaginative kingdom of 'Terebithia' in abandoned woods by their homes, a world filled with trolls, exotic creatures and talking animals. But when reality soon seeks to crash down on the children's world, changing their lives forever, can Jesse hold on to the magic of Terebithia...The child actors in this film were phenomenal and carried the story with the grace of veteran actors who had decades of experience under their belts. Josh Hutcherson was excellent as Jesse, beautifully depicting how disenchanted the character was with life initially as he vied for the attention of a busy father and fought to make himself stand out from his sisters and classmates yet recaptured a boyish sense of joy through his friendship with Leslie. He also handled the darker scenes with remarkable poignancy. AnnaSophia Robb, in her role of Leslie, was no lead weight either. She gave a very likable performance and was perfect in depicting her character's heartfelt spirited-nature, without comprising the sense of vulnerability that clung to the character. Little Bailee Madison, as Jesse's five-year-old sister May Belle, definitely deserves a mention who was not only adorable but gave a genuinely captivating performance as Jesse's most loyal 'supporter'. Robert Patrick, one of the few adult actors to stand out in what is very much the child actors' film, was notable in his role as Jesse's father, a man who believed in showing his children the importance of hard-work, not realising his aloof nature was distancing his son from him, yet who did love his family very much even if he couldn't always demonstrate that effectively.The problem with this film was that it was marketed as if it was a fantasy-lite flick in the vein of 'Harry Potter' or 'The Lion, The Witch and the Wardrobe' when it is much more a coming-of-age film similar, in many ways, to 'My Girl', 'Jack the Bear' and 'Wide Awake'. The magic creatures and fantastic kingdom of Terebithia is only a small part of Jesse's journey. The primary thread of 'The Bridge to Terebithia' is about a boy standing on the cusp of puberty, the bridge between childhood and adulthood, and having to learn the harsh realities of life without letting go of his belief in magic and the jubilance of embracing his imagination.And, as a coming-of-age film, this succeeds very well in teaching children that, even if there is a darker side to the world, it doesn't mean it has to be a terrible place to live while also leaving adult viewers nostalgic for the time when they were Jesse's age and learning these lessons. If only Disney had the guts to produce more films like this instead of repetitive drudge they seem to enjoy oozing out for kids these days.This is definitely a highly recommended film for the family. A word of warning to parents. This film is rated 'PG', which means 'parental guidance', as in watch it first before deciding on whether it is suitable for your very young and/or sensitive children.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>Never has simplicity been so beautiful</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>To those who have not encountered the book, the trailer of Terabithia is criminally misleading, having you believe that this is another Narnia story of kids stumbling into a fantasyland. But if that is what it takes to bring the audience into the theatre, I'll give it a "not guilty" verdict, as the movie is definitely worth seeing. No Narnia though. Terabithia is more comparable to "Pan's Labyrinth" in structure, in children escaping from unhappiness of reality into an imaginative fantasy world. It is more like a very brief slice in the life of a 10-year-old boy. Unlike the devastating experience of Ofelia in "Pan's Labyrinth" during a cruel war, the experience of Jesse is quite ordinary, with the "villains" being no worse than bullies that all of us have encountered in school, and misfortune no wore than being born in a poor family (from which came, incidentally, many great men). Out of this ordinary life, however, comes an episode that becomes the memory of a lifetime. In its deceptive simplicity, the movie covers so many different elements that give you so much to reflect on.It is worth repeating that what we see in the movie is ordinary, even if it will disappoint those audience whose capacity to appreciate simple things has been completely wrecked by images of a hopelessly distorted world some movie makers present, out of incompetence to impress an audience with anything better than shock, shock and more shock. Spice and more spicy spice, sweets and sweeter sweets will eventually destroy the taste bud entirely. One critic comments that watching this movie is like taking in a drink of pure water from a fresh spring.To say more would take away some of the pleasures of watching this movie. Suffices to say that it is at once simple and complex because of the loving attention given to simple feelings we often ignore. There is no pretense to sophisticated emotions or things like Freudian complexes. All the emotions presented simply and honestly in this movie we can recognize easily from our daily lives. That is what makes this movie so endearing.The movie rests on the two lead, Josh Hutcherson and AnnaSophia Robb, at their early teens playing 5th graders. They are marvelous. There is also a wonderful supporting cast.</fullReview>

		<username>Simon Parker</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>A Bridge that Opens Up Your Mind</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>The focus at the moment is very much upon fantasy based novels. Anything remotely fantasy based is currently being snatched up by the big name studios in order for them to make a profit. After Lord of the Rings scored big, Chronicles of Narnia and Harry Potter scored lots of money as well, loads of novels rights have been bought. Currently in production we have the first in the His Dark Materials series, another series likely to make a large sum of money. So what about Bridge to Terabithia. Us folks in England have pretty much never heard of this book, but apparently it was extremely popular in America many years ago. My initial feelings towards Bridge to Terabithia is that it would be just another Narnia knock off. That was the way the trailers made it out to be, and every TV Spot I saw did the same. So what a surprise to say that this really is not that much of a fantasy film. It has fantasy elements in it, but there is actually little time spent in the magical land of Terabithia. Instead this is very much a drama, a drama about friendship and the power of imagination. Its only very rarely we get treated to the site of a magical creature in the make believe world of Terabithia, but those moments aren't the ones that stick in memory. Its the smaller, more powerful moments that really stick in the mind. Come the surprisingly tragic finale the focus of the movie has shifted, most of the audience I saw this with were reduced to tears. Its a powerful conclusion and one that makes this easily one of the best family movies I have ever seen.So lets first start with the actors of the movie. Child actors are usually pretty awful, Daniel Radcliffe, Edward Speleers, at times Haley Joel Osment and loads more. Most are one hit wonders and then disappear. Most are also eye gougingly annoying. So what a huge surprise to say that Josh Hutcherson and Anna Sophia Robb are two of the most talented young actors I have ever seen. They have a level of maturity and chemistry between them that makes them believable. Each character has their own flaws, and the actors play on them brilliantly. The scenes where they simply talk are memorable because these two actors really can act. They both have a bright and promising career ahead of them. The adult actors of course never get the time to breath because the focus is very much on the child actors. However Zooey Deschanel and Robert Patrick make the most of their brief screen time, making two very interesting and also believable characters.Its the movies story that really does stay in memory though. Its a simple tale about two children who become unlikely friends. The two then decided to create their own special place for themselves, and thus in their minds form the magical land of Terabithia. That's really it, well there is more in the final quarter of the movie but can't ruin that for you as the impact will softened. Its a simple tale and all the more effective for it, for a movie being passed off as a Narnia knock off it always seems a better movie. Surprising as this has no huge epic battle at the end to wow audiences, this is a movie purely about a friendship and its also one that you can't help but be moved by. This is easily one of the best family movies of all time, and despite it no doubt going to be ignored at the cinema, it will hopefully have a long life on DVD.So are there any faults then, well at times the CGI isn't amazing, thankfully the CGI is kept very low due to their being few times we actually see Terabithia. Also this isn't for people who go in a movie expecting huge battles, this is no Lord of the Rings or Narnia, this is something a lot different. While its not as good as Lord of the Rings it is a lot more impressive than Narnia. Apart from that I saw no faults, it has a great running time and superb performances. This is a movie that will undoubtedly feature in the top 10 of 2007 at the end of year. A great movie, a shame it will be shunned aside by the vastly inferior Spiderman 3 currently showing at the cinemas, but Terabithia is the much better movie and one that sticks in memory for a long time.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>One of the best family films ever</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>This film challenges and charms its audience with its lovely tale of love and growing up. Buried in it, it is a world that is open to those who are willing to close their eyes and let their imagination wander. A young boy befriends a newcomer to his grey and stressful world. She opens new doors to a new world full of love, friendship, and some quite wonderful creations.The film moves on, presenting a variety of relationships between the boy and his teachers, his family, and his new friend. As we are expecting to be fully transported to the world they are creating, something tragic happens, and the audience had better get ready to confront an intense painful moment, as the main character tries to cope with new changes.In spite of its strong, realistic themes, the film is a wonderful addition to classics that don't hesitate to explore reality in creative ways. Much of the credit should go to the young protagonist and the marvelous job done by the director. A great film.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Not what I expected...but not great either</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Let me first start off by saying that I have read Bridge To Terabithia. I was in fourth grade and loved it. The book is a story about friendship and loss. It was beautifully written, but so easy to destroy if some producers decided to make a movie out of it. They could create romance between Leslie and Jesse. They could do a numerous amount of things that would make fans of the book not want to see the movie.When I saw the trailer, I literally thought, "Okay, did these people read the book or did they only hear about a made up world called Terabithia and decided to run away with it?" Fans of the book, you don't have to worry about Bridge To Terabithia becoming a fantasy adventure. The people who create the trailers didn't do their job too well. They might have thought that by adding fantasy into the trailers would make younger kids want to see it. Well, they screwed up. Not only did it make fans of the book stay away from it, when others went to see a movie that they expected to be fantasy, they were sorely disappointed. The fantasy creatures are only what the two children, Leslie and Jesse are imagining in their made up world. They *don't* have to "save Terabithia" from these monsters, as one trailer claimed. Don't believe the trailers.The movie itself is about two children who appear to be in the fifth grade. Jesse Aarons is somewhat of a country boy. He has four sisters and his family is having financial trouble.He doesn't always get along with his dad or his sisters. He is the fastest runner in his grade, but gets picked on by bullies and has a jerk for a teacher-but a nice music teacher.Enter Leslie Burke, a young, pretty, unique girl whose parents write fantasy novels for a living. She has a great imagination and a close family (she's an only child). Leslie also gets picked on bullies for being different. She and her family move in a house that is close to Jesse's. She replaces Jesse as the fastest runner, which, in a way, brings them together. To escape the problems of the outside world, they find a place that only they know about, and that only they can cross-by swinging on an old rope over the river. Once they are across, they are in Terabithia, a forest filled with trolls and creatures of Light and Darkness from their imagination. Over the course of the movie, problems arise, but Leslie and Jesse deal with them and continue to come back to Terabithia. Until one day, after a lot of rain, Leslie tries to cross over into Teribithia without Jesse. The rope swing snaps, Leslie hits her head, and drowns. I'll leave the rest open.Problems that I had with this movie seem to be never ending. Hutcherson (who plays Jesse) had on-off acting. Sometimes he was decent, other times...not so much. Robb (who plays Leslie) was much better, in my opinion. Madison (who plays May Belle was actually very good considering her age.I would have liked Ms. Edmonds to have had a bigger role, and a bigger impact on Jesse. It seemed like she wasn't that important.The dialog was very shaky at times. Especially the bullies' insults, which were supposed to make you feel sympathy for the kid being teased, just made me laugh. It was stupid. No other word for it. Some of the conversations between Jesse and Leslie seemed unrealistic as well.This movie didn't really have any lesson to it. We don't really learn about death or how to cope with it. The only thing I got out of this movie was from my friend Maria who was sitting next to me. At some point during the movie, she laughed out loud, and the popcorn she was eating almost went out her nose. The only thing I learned from this movie was, "Popcorn feels *really* weird coming out your nose." A bit of wisdom that I didn't really need to know about.The one thing that really got to me was the scenes of Leslie and Jesse running through the woods together, playing and having fun with their imaginations. I know that sounds cheesy, but five years ago I was doing that too, and Bridge To Terabithia made me want to go grab my brother and sister and play with them in the backyard. It really did bring back heartfelt memories. That, and the reason I was prejudiced against this movie even before I saw it is the reason I gave it four stars.Don't go see this movie in theaters. Fans of the book, you might want to give it a try. Maybe. It actually does stay pretty true to it. Rent the movie if you're bored. Maybe you'll like it more than I did.-Sarah</fullReview>

		<username>dutchs-1</username>
		<score>0.1</score>
		<shortDescription>Close to Consumer Fraud</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>What's worse than spending an evening at a movie that was completely different than you'd been led to expect? Coming home and having your intelligence insulted by an IMDb reviewer who claimed that disappointed viewers hadn't "researched" the film well enough. I wonder if this reviewer would write it off as "inadequate research" if he found his car's odometer had been reset, the "natural" foods he'd bought were full of additives, or the house he'd bought was full of concealed termite damage.We've all seen movies where we've said all the good stuff is in the trailers. Never has it been so literally true as with this movie. Essentially all the visual wonder and fantasy is in the trailers. Beyond that, there literally is nothing else in the film. We all know trailers hype the best scenes of a film, but to put out trailers that mislead so completely borders on consumer fraud. Putting this film in the same class as "Narnia" is like calling "Blood Diamond" a musical comedy, or "Bruce Almighty" a psychological thriller.I first suspected trouble when Zooey Deschanel showed up as the music teacher in school. Not that I have any problems with Zooey Deschanel. Far from it. But when someone of her billing turns up on the real world side of a fantasy film, there are only two ways to go. Either she'll also be a character in the alternative universe, or there won't BE an alternative universe. The film goes the second route.The plot is a stock plot of bright imaginative nonconformists dealing with school bullies. There's also a plot line where Jess, the hero, has to deal with his loutish father, more or less copied verbatim from "October Sky." At one point the father tells his son "You've got your head in the clouds." Fat lot of good "common sense" has done the father. In prosperous farm country, he can't make ends meet with both a farm and a second job. Mebbe if he'd got hisself some of thet thar book l'arnin', he might just figure out that a "farm" has to be more than a greenhouse with a few tomato plants. The scene where the father consoles his son is a classic of what I call "Nazi With A Puppy Dog" cinema, an attempt to humanize an otherwise repulsive character by showing him in a tender moment. I'm sure Hitler loved his dog, too.This being a Disney film, we were at least spared all the adolescent sexual discovery clichés, although considering the other themes the film was developing, I half expected it at any moment.Considered as an adolescent coming of age film, it maybe rates a six. There are a few good moments. Leslie, the new girl in school, is marvelous, although I don't picture someone of her looks and personality being an outsider. One of the bullies has at least a bit of a character transformation. (Nice touch: compare the bully's face with the troll in the fantasy) Considered as a fantasy film full of visual wonder, it rates a zero. It just isn't that kind of film and promoting it that way is little short of criminal.By trying to be two wildly different things, the movie fails to be either. As a film about two kids coping with bullies and retreating to a secret fantasy world, it might have come out a bit like "Secret Garden." And of course it could have been a full blown fantasy adventure. But by jerking back and forth from one mode to the other, it shortchanges both story lines.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<fullReview>I remember seeing the trailer for this film and it looked so captivating I decided to see it for real accompanied by two support staff and a housemate from my former care home. While the incidental music is pretty forgettable, the most memorable songs are 'Why Can't We Be Friends?' and 'Someday (as sung by Jess's class)' and AnnaSophia Robb's solo number over the end credits. The film mostly stayed true to the book (which I read after watching this film) albeit its periodical differences (for example, in the book, Jess and Leslie's class are required to watch a Jacques Cousteau documentary whereas in the film the documentary is about Bob Ballard). I also came across the Nostalgia Critic's review for this fairly recently and while he panned a couple of outdated elements, an insensitive comment from one of the bullies after Leslie's passing plus the overly-whimsical nature of Terabithia, he found Leslie's death and its aftermath handled maturely. I agree with him about the death scene being well-handled and the bully telling Jess he is the fastest kid in the class but I pretty much disagreed with everything else that was criticised in the review.Overall, this is a magical and captivating film despite its emotionally intense moments. 8/10.</fullReview>

		<username>gasmaskproductionsbooks (gasmaskproductionsbooks@gmail.com)</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Totally Unforgettable</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>It isn't very often that you find such complex and original characters in a kid's film, but Bridge to Terabithia is a strange, depressing and yet beautiful and hopeful film that honestly every kid (and adult too) should be required to watch.The plot seems innocent enough; Jess' family is on the verge of total poverty and they live in a small town appearing to take place in the 1970's-1980's. I'm not entirely certain since a few background kids had cellular phones. Anyway, Jess is always the target of bullying, has annoying sisters and gets second-hand girl's shoes from his older sister. His parents are strict and he thinks he's just a boring kid with no future, until he meets Leslie, a nonconformist girl who has hippie-like parents and doesn't watch television, much to the astonishment of her new classmates. She starts spending time in the woods with Jess, to live in their imaginary world, Terabithia. Meanwhile they befriend a caring music teacher and learn that bullies are often troubled at home, when the biggest school bully, Janice, gets beat by her dad and abused.When a sudden tragedy destroys their friendship forever, Jess has to decide how he wants to spend the remainder of his teenage years. However, Leslie's fatal accident teaches him several lessons, and much to his surprise, Janice the bully starts being nice to him, his crabby teacher bursts into tears in front of him and confesses her feelings of grief for her deceased husband, and Jess' father finally expresses how much he loves Jess.Parents today like to keep the topic of death away from kids, which isn't totally a bad thing, but it leaves them unprepared. Many kids lose someone sooner or later, whether it's a friend, pet, family member or neighbor, it can leave an imprint on them forever. I never got over my best friend's murder when I was fifteen and I doubt I ever will. This film proves though that from death you can still love a person and not take their memory in vain by taking the lessons they gave you and giving to another person's life. Leslie's death is somewhat disturbing, but this isn't a horror film, her death isn't shown on-screen, just talked about later on.The film isn't just about dealing with grief, it's about getting through hard times, family matters, dealing with bullies and hearing both sides to every story. The characters are very realistic and the soundtrack is amazing (thank god this film hasn't been touched by pop music). Bailee Madison from the popular TV series The Haunting Hour was great in the role of Jess' little sister May Belle, in fact the acting was generally very excellent, especially when you consider that many of the actors/actresses were kids and teens.There are some stories about real friendship that have stayed with me. The Lovely Bones by Alice Sebold, No Place for Eco-Sinners by Racheal Bates, Becoming Chloe by Cathrine Hyde, and Mr. Death's Blue Eyed Girls by Mary Hahn. I only hope that if these books are made to films they'll be as amazing as Bridge to Terabithia.</fullReview>

		<score>0.9</score>
		<shortDescription>Powerful.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>"So I realize that if it's hard for me, how much harder it must be for you."There are very few movies that inspire a genuine emotional response from me. Something beyond the superficial momentary humor, happiness, and sadness that is the basis of so many films. Movies like The Wrestler, Million Dollar Baby, and Forrest Gump all take the viewer beyond the passive experience of watching, to the active experience of feeling exactly what the characters are feeling. Bridge to Terabithia is most definitely another one of those movies. I kid you not when I tell you that the last part of the movie left me stunned in a way that took me quite a while to get over.&nbsp;It's also one of the best films about what being a kid is actually like. Dealing with issues that adults can't even handle well, like loss and loneliness and problems at home. And it handles those issues in an adult way that pushes Bridge to Terabithia far beyond the label of "kid's movie". Sure, it's about friendship and imagination and other topics that are the cornerstones of movies for kids, but those subjects are only the tip of the iceberg.&nbsp;There isn't much fault to find with it, beyond the heavy emotional toll it may take on those who are too young or unprepared to deal with the subject matter. There are a few unnecessary and non-mainstream ideas about Christianity that the movie would have been better served by leaving out, but I can't find fault with anything else. The cast was great, the special effects were imaginative and well done, and all the elements combined together in manner that just felt "right". This is a sweet, genuine, and heartbreaking story that should be seen by anyone and everyone who has the emotional maturity to handle it.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Bridge to Terabithia</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>From the trailer I saw, I thought this was going to be some sort of Chronicles of Narnia rip-off, but it was actually surprisingly good. Basically ten-year-old Jesse 'Jess' Aarons (Josh Hutcherson) lives with his poor family, father Jack (Robert Patrick), mother Mary (Kate Butler), and four annoying sisters, in a farm house. He has a love for drawing, is bullied at school and has hardly any friends, and then he meets the new ten-year-old girl student who beats him in a race. Jess and Leslie Burke (Charlie and the Chocolate Factory's AnnaSophia Robb) have a rocky start, but she doesn't let bullies bother her, and being neighbours, they become very close friends. One day they find a rope swing across a near dried out river, and swinging to the other side, Leslie starts claiming they are in a magical land with many mythical creatures living in it. Jess eventually gets into this imagined world also, and they name it Terabithia, to have some amazing adventures with monsters, trolls, ogres, and giants, with him and Leslie as the king and queen. Their friendship also leads them to give the bullies a taste of their own medicine, and Jess's love of drawing is an interest to his attractive teacher Ms. Edmunds (Yes Man's Zooey Deschanel), who one day invites him to an art gallery. When tragedy occurs, Leslie dying when the rope swing snaps, Jess blames himself for her death, and only has his parents and younger sister May Belle Aarons (Bailee Madison) to comfort him. In the end though, he misses Terabithia, and decides to make a magical bridge, to return to the land he rules, with May Belle as his princess to join in the imagination. Also starring Devon Wood as Brenda Aarons, Emma Fenton as Ellie Aarons, Grace Brannigan as Joyce Aarons and Latham Gaines as Bill Burke. Hutcherson and Robb are wonderful as the leading child stars, and the special effects are marvellous to take you into the realm of imagination, a great family fantasy adventure. Very good!</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Wonderful film - not at all what I was expecting!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>This movie really defied my expectations and I would agree with some comments that the advertising does not prepare you very well for the nature of the film itself. However it seems that the promotions department is just about the only element of the production team that didn't get it right (one can only assume that the advertising was done by a generic Disney team rather than the film makers themselves - it's the only trace of anything Disneyesque in the movie) This is a quite, quite wonderful movie that stays with you for a long time after the first viewing. Any connections to a Narnia type story should be forgotten as in some ways it is closer to Pans Labyrinth in the way that it deals with real world issues through escapist fantasy. Another film that it evokes is "Stand by Me" in that it deals with the trials and difficulties encountered by children who don't quite "fit in" as they grow up and the importance (and depth) of childhood friendships.The focus is on the young lead characters but this in no way means that it is a specifically children's movie. It is rather a true family movie that adults will enjoy just as much and in some ways the depth of emotion will be lost on young children (recommended for 10+). The director shows how the worlds of the adults and children brush against each other with great insight and subtlety. This is a really well crafted piece of cinema where the pictures and images convey the reality of family life rather than sentimental dialogue.The "look" of the film is excellent, with first class editing and cinematography. The quality of the acting from the young leads is outstanding and the director has done an excellent job in extracting such natural and honest performances from them. The writing is also restrained and well crafted with no gushing or indulgent sentimentality. For all its reference to imaginative escapism - it is the moments of reality that really hit home.At a time when Hollywood seems bereft of ideas and is simply churning out lame franchise sequels this is an excellent exception that really deserves a much larger audience. A word of caution to parents: don't watch this without a child - you'll need them to hold your hand all through the final third of this impressive movie!</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>As others have noted: This was a misrepresented movie</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I just felt the need to add my voice to the many other reviewers that felt that this movie was 'misrepresented'. I do not want to counter anyone that did like the movie, because I am not saying that Bridge to Terabithia was a 'bad' movie. I am simply saying that it is NOT the movie that was advertised.I can actually summarize, very briefly, my whole issue with this movie: The advertisement for this movie was tailored in such a way that it leads the audience to believe that it is a light hearted fantasy movie about some teenage characters that travel to the mystical world of Terabithia, have adventures and meet fairy tale beings.However, that is not true. Instead the movie is actually a drama about a teenage boy, his relationship with his new friend and how he copes with the death of his friend.Imagine going to see a rip-roaring action movie, because the trailers showed all manner of 'action' scenes. But when you watch the movie, you find out that it is really a romance/drama movie and the 'action' scenes shown in the trailers were only daydreams that one of the main character had.As a drama movie, it was okay (I would rate it 5/10). However, as a fantasy/adventure movie that I was led to believe I would be seeing, I rate it 1/10.</fullReview>

A cynical layer of myself would say it's too childish and can be seen through. But the truth elicited in Terabithia shows that each layer is at once important and ridiculous, and underneath this lies what a true open mind is: one that is not afraid to admit that everyone must be right, that everyone must be wrong, that for now, this is all complete garbage. 		<fullReview>Its march break and the kids wanted to see a movie. Its an extraordinarily intelligent film that is clever and authentic. Nothing seemed forced. The acting was fantastic! Everything rang true. I especially loved the boys reluctance to fantasize.What an amazingly refreshing story. I think part of the basis of selecting a great movie is that you don't know what is going to happen next. A great movie should always leave you guessing... but not with gimmicks (like the 6th sense), but by utilizing truly original story telling methods.Unlike Narnia, this film never loses it grounding in reality. Rather the fantasy world is just as the edge of the story, there for escape, fun, an adventure, but the kids are still in the real world where real problems occur.Is this film for children? I took my boys. They watched it from beginning to end without fuss (quite a feat for a group of boys) -- they didn't even need a bathroom break. My eldest (a teen) hated it, but the other two (7 and 10) enjoyed it. My youngest has been drawing pictures and writing stories ever since. Its a film that treats youths as capable of the full range of emotions.. No hint of any patronizing attitude towards youth. As such I think its something that children will not only appreciate, but will grow from having experienced it.To the overly concerned parents afraid of showing kids "anti-social" messages such as parents that get angry and the tragedy of death -- get real -- don't patronize the kids. Life is not a fun filled fantasy where ever parent is perfect, bullies don't exist, and no one dies. I think films that show perfect people do a terrible disservice to society by setting up false expectations. Life is not perfect. This was an honest to goodness tragedy (in the Shakespearean sense) -- it was sad, but there is a lot we can learn from tragedy. Understanding tragedy make us better prepared for life. Because of this need for sugar coated silly films, there are so few really good tragedies in modern films. What puzzles me is that people compare it to Narnia. Narnia was a terribly violent film which had great animation, but little else. But both are about kids using fantasy to deal with stress. OK. But the reality is that fantasy no matter how useful it is, does not actually allow you to go into an other world -- and that is the case in the film. Compared to Narnia this is a much much better film.But don't go if all you want is another silly fantasy.</fullReview>

		<date>2007-06-18</date>
		<username>Polaris_DiB</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>An idyllic elegy</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>When I went around breathlessly telling everybody about this movie after I saw it, I was met with skepticism, cynicism, and especially a direct correlation of those-who-saw-the-trailer to those-who-didn't-want-to-see-it. I need to state this right out, before all other comments on this movie: the trailer was awful, and this movie is not a Chronicles of Narnia-style vehicle for Disney. Sharing thematic elements with Narnia (the book mentions this connection as well), this is a story about friendship and grief, and it is highly personal, beautiful, and endearing. It is, in fact, one of the best children's movies I have ever seen.Gabor Csupo (of Nickelodeon animation fame) endows these children's lives with light and shadow, personal moments, and telling faith, while the children return the favor by doing some of the best acting of the year. Anna Sophia Robb has more charisma and chemistry than the world's leading actors, and it's hard not to believe that these two children aren't in love with each other, which is what makes the story so much more painful.Bridge to Terabithia is a story about a ten year old farmer boy named Jess, caught among four sisters, bullied by the regular crew of hurtful bullies, and generally just wanting to spend his time drawing, when a new girl-next-door named Leslie ruins everything--she becomes his best friend, and they design an escapist realm called "Terabithia" in the woods behind their houses, an area of play and abstraction pretty much exactly like my experiences as a kid in the woods, only a bit wetter. The first five minutes, are, perhaps, an exercise in children's-movie contrivance, with all of the more overt and unrealistic styles of verbal abuse of the other children, but once Jess gets past his initial distrust of Leslie and the two become friends, the film transcends itself into a realm of imagination more poignant (and tellingly more simple) than the line of contemporary fantasy currently being produced.This movie is both an idyll and an elegy, combining a poetic sense of the world and a love of a child's viewpoint with a deep understanding of the pain and reality of both. In other words, it's surprising for Disney--no wonder they mis-marketed it, it's actually worth something! In this movie are theological discussions, realizations of love, heavy moments of pain, and an uncanny personal connection, all things that have been mismanaged or done poorly a thousand times before, but that Csupo finally gets right. He gets into these character's heads better than any adult ever could visually, and even has command of devices like foreshadowing and symbolism often never seen beyond the art-film circuit.After seeing this movie, I immediately spent another two hours reading the book. It, too, uses it's methods appropriately and details a world and a story poignantly and majestically. "Bridge to Terabithia" is a story that should be experienced, in whatever form, for it is a beautiful and loving ode to the experiences that define childhood and growing up.--PolarisDiB</fullReview>
	</review>

It gives the perspective of how one's imagination can lead to the befriending of two mismatched people like Jesse and Leslie and how it improves one's life. This movie reminds children how complicated life can be and how letting your imagination guide you can go a long way. 		<username>p-stepien</username>
		<score>0.7</score>
		<shortDescription>Well bridged to the target</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>"Bridge to Terrabithia", a deservedly beautiful and charming adaptation of the source material by Katherine Patterson, delivers a somewhat poignant story bound to capture the target audience by the heart. The story's main protagonist Jess Aarons (Josh Hutcherson) lives on the countryside with his financially-stressed family, at times lacking required warmth and care from his crass father Jack (Robert Patrick). Somewhat of a school loner, often targeted by school bullies, Jess hardly has any friends, hence spending most of his time and creative energy in drawing fantasy worlds or googling at his beautiful music teacher Ms Edmunds (Zooey Deschanel). When a family of writers moves next door, Jess quickly finds a common language with the spirited and independent-minded Leslie Burke (AnnaSophia Robb). Together they indulge into their own world of imagination across a local stream - a fairy land inhabited by trolls, creatures of light and dark, in which the duo self-proclaim themselves king and queen. This inner world of fantasy soon transcends into their everyday life...The movie, now slowly turning into a classic, possibly failed to prove a financial success due to the heavy themes of death, passing, acceptance of loss and a rejection of close-minded views of others, which make it a much more laden story to tell, than parents or children normally expect. Especially given the story is actually pretty sparse on magical creatures and extraordinary adventures, much below what even I personally expected. Fronted by two tremendously well played characters - with Robb especially capturing the eye with some astoundingly charismatic presence - "Road to Terrabithia" manages to captivate attention, immediately warming up to the audience.Devoid of a simplistic purely positive outlook on live or intense CGI fuelled visuals, this movie may prove one of those unexpected first adventures into the tougher realities of life. Where bullies aren't pure evil. Where first loves must be lived. And where death must be accepted. All well converged to a language well adjusted to its target audience of young teens. Truly inspirational watching, which is bound even to entice the more sarcastic outlook of adults, forcing them to reminisce with their own moments of coming of age.Nonetheless, the opening third of the movie drags slowly, failing to pick up tempo and leaving an overwhelming feeling that some initial opportunities had been loss to better build the background to Jess and Leslie. Also I had the intense feeling that modern standards of youth-oriented films fail to prepare youth to a darker take on reality, thus making it a somewhat unwanted treasure by those who truly should immerse into the message it offers. Maybe a bit more pizazz to liven up proceedings could have made audience better acclimatise to the heavy laden issues lurking around the script corner? Nonetheless, this is a minor question, not faulting the pretty adventurous direction chosen by director Gabor Csupo, who truly focused on the content, bigger picture, not on delivering an enthralling picturesque extravaganza, which is easy for the eyes and the mind.</fullReview>
	</review>

Using their imaginations, they create a magical fantasy world they call Terabithia, and the rope swing across the river serves as a "bridge". On the subtext, you have a film that's about living free and exploring your mind, and not being afraid to take risks and go for something new.What also stands out in this movie is the talent of two excellent young actors, Josh Hutcherson (Zathura and Firehouse Dog), and especially Annasophia Robb (Because of Winn Dixie and Jumper). The movie also features Robert Patrick as Hutcherson's father and Zooey Deschanel as a teacher. It was marketed as a big fantasy adventure like Harry Potter, Narnia, or The Golden Compass, but it's a realistic journey about two kids who are discovering themselves and their fantastic fun along the way. Parents, this movie is a wonderful story to show your children, and I give it the highest recommendation I can.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Beautiful, charming and touching fantasy film</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Based on Katherine Patterson's beautiful book, Bridge to Terabithia is a beautiful, charming and touching fantasy film, that serves as an emotionally rich testament to the life-changing power of friendship. The film does start off a little slow, as the two protagonists at first interact quite awkwardly, but fifteen minutes in the pacing picked up. I was pleasantly surprised by how quickly the film went. The story is quite simple, as Jess and Leslie encounter mundane daily experiences and become inseparable as a result by their alienation and creativity, but it is an effective one and respects reasonably the story of the book. Also the script ensures that the characters are believable; Jess and Leslie certainly are believable as characters, and Gabor Csupo, who also directed the surprisingly good and underrated Secret of Moonacre, tackles the issues explored in the film with wit and sensitivity.Visually and technically, I couldn't fault Bridge to Terabithia. Moonacre is a little better in the costume and sets department but Terabithia succeeds much better in the depth and character departments. Here the cinematography is fluid, the scenery is stunning and the costumes are very nice. Terabithia itself is like a homage to CS Lewis's Chronicles of Narnia and is very attractive, the final shot of the film was like looking at a painting and the creatures while you don't see much of them are pretty much fantastical. The music score I have to say was beautiful, with a soaring main theme and some other pretty tunes to add to the film's charm.And of course the performances are wonderful. Josh Hutcherson is absolutely brilliant as Jess, he was truly believable and his acting in the final segment was close to heart breaking. AnnaSophia Robb is enchanting as Leslie, she looked lovely and acted with a lot of heart. Her character's death people complained of bringing down the film. I had no problem with it, while it was deeply affecting the way the actors and director brought it across gave the scene itself and the scenes afterwards a real sense of poignancy. Is it just me though, or don't Hutcherson and Robb have great chemistry together? I think so, their chemistry for me was what made the film so charming. The lovely Zooey Deschannel isn't given as much to do, but she has a relevant role to the film which she delivers with a sensitivity and luminosity that I never knew she had. And Robert Patrick is a great actor, and gives another great performance as the gruff and no nonsense father. Plus Bailie Maddison is really cute as Jess's sister.Overall, a really good film. Shame the advertising was so misleading. 9/10 Bethany Cox</fullReview>
